text:
I adore biscuits and have been trying to find the perfect recipe.  This one comes very close.  In the name of science I made three versions of this recipe one evening; one with all shortening, one with half shortening and half butter, and one with all butter.  The recipe with all shortening was very bland.  The half butter recipe was very good and the texture was incredible.  They were almost melt in your mouth tender.  The all butter taste was slightly better, but the texture wasn't as nice.   I also use my food processor to mix the dry ingredients and to cut in the butter, but you have to be careful not to process it too much.  (Leaving large chunks of butter makes them flakier.) I transfer the flour mixture to a bowl and stir in the milk.     I also took a batch of dough and kneaded half of it 20 times and didn't knead the other half (my mom always taught me that kneading biscuits made them tougher).  Surprise! The kneaded dough rose almost twice as tall when the biscuits were baked.   Also, rolling them out so they are an 1 inch thick makes them even taller too.

text:
This is the recipe we always use for biscuits now!  I do a couple of things differently after a LOT of trial and error.  I use COLD butter in place of the shortening and cut back just a little on the salt.  Then, instead of rolling and cutting the dough, I use my ice cream scoop, which makes perfectly  even biscuits, each and every time.  I place them on a greased cookie sheet and lightly press the tops down to flatten a little.  I've brushed the tops with butter, cream, egg wash, milk...you name it.  Anyway you want to top them, these are AWESOME biscuits!...and they have ALWAYS turned out!

text:
Fantastic. I think using ALL shortening is the quintessential factor in true, southern biscuits. Shortening creates an extremely flaky, tender crumb.  But I agree it lacks flavor without butter.  I always use 1 full teaspoon of salt when using all shortening and Butter flavored shortening is preferable over plain.  I do NOT knead this 20 times as stated.  I knead this about 3-4 times just enough to bring the dough together before gently patting it out for cutting.  This light handling keeps the biscuits light, with fluffy layers.  Overworking the dough will create a tough, dense biscuit.  Roll it out thick, about 2 inches, for a nice thick biscuit.  I brush the tops with cream, milk or eggs before baking for nice color and shine. (Cream & Milk will give the best shine) This recipe makes just 5 biscuits, so doubling it for company is a good idea.  Easy recipe for even you beginner bakers! This is my master biscuit recipe. (12 min. bake time for 5 biscuits, 2 in. thick)

Best biscuits we've ever made.

text:
Excellent! After all the positive reviews, I was convinced to get up and make these first thing this morning for breakfast. I increased the sugar to 1T and used 1 tsp of salt. Instead of shortening I used butter and 2/3 cup of buttermilk. I kneaded the dough, rolled into 1 inch thickness and used a cup to cut out the biscuits. In a short time, I had 12 round biscuits placed upon a greased baking sheet. I brushed the top with a little melted butter right before placing them into the oven. I only had to bake these biscuits for 9 minutes. They rose up and expanded nicely. The buttery fragrance was so intense it made my mouth water while these baked. About 6 minutes into the baking, I saw a light brown color forming on top of the biscuits. As soon as the timer went off, I opened the oven to take the biscuits out and I got a nice whiff of buttery scent. I am so pleased with the way these turned out. The title of these biscuits fit perfectly - FLUFFY! They are not only fluffy, but moist, buttery and delicious! They feel light, taste tender and melts in my mouth.  From the smell, the appearance and taste this was just awesome good! I spread a little guava jelly on top of the warm biscuits thou' they could be eaten just by itself they are so flavorful! If you are thinking about baking these, try them! They are that good! I served these along with, "Breakfast Sausage," also from this website. All 12 biscuits were completely wiped out within minutes. That tells me a lot!!!

text:
I'm not a biscuit maker. My husband is from the south and *loves* biscuits. Sadly, I make them every few years; sadder still is they're just shy of  awful.  I found this recipe and boy, did I WOW my husband with these. It had been so long since the last time I made biscuits that I think he forgot my poor biscuiting skills. He took one bite of these flaky, layered, high as the sky, made for TV biscuits and looked at me lovingly and said, "You make the BEST biscuits.", like it was a historical fact. Yes, they're that good; they gave my husband biscuit amnesia. I basked in the undeserved glory. This is one of those recipes I'm going to memorize. Love it.

*I made these twice. The first batch I put salt in it and used Land O' Lakes salted butter.  They came out too salty. I'm a salt nut too. The next time I omitted the salt but still used the salted butter. They came out even better. ** IMPORTANT** Also I read the reviews and I think it was J West who said she uses cold, cold butter, cut up and pulsed into the dry ingredients in her food processor. I did just that, then kneaded the dough only 20 times, rolled and cut to about 1 inch thick. I think this was a key to the yumminess of these biscuits. Holy guacamole. THESE biscuits give me a free pass into the South. Seriously. They're THAT good.

text:
This recipe is a snap to put together in a food processor.  And the end result is a buttery, fluffy, flaky pillow of deliciousness!  I always substitute the shortening with butter.  Simply put all dry engredients into the bowl of your processor and pulse a few times to sift.  Cut one stick of butter into 12 or so pats and distribute them evenly on top of the flour mixture.  Pulse a few times to cut the butter into the flour.  Mix your egg and milk together in a separate bowl, then just dump it into the processor with the flour.  Pulse a few more times to create the dough.  Then turn the dough out onto a floured surface and knead as instructed.  We don't care what our biscuits look like, so I just roll them out and then cut them into squares.  Easy peasy!  These only take me about 10 minutes to throw together in this manner and they are always delicious!

Alright ..so here's the deal...I've been using JP's Big Daddy Biscuits recipe from this site for a while now, and I thought they were pretty darn tasty...until I came across THIS recipe! Oh my goodness, these are perfect with a capital "P".  I used half shortening/half salted butter, and just patted the dough instead of kneading it. I discovered that tip from my other recipe, I guess it helps them rise more :~)

text:
I have made this recipe several times over the last four months. They are the fluffiest biscuits I have ever made, but I much prefer using butter rather than shortening, which is why I gave it four stars instead of five. There is such a difference in the taste. Depending on how the biscuits were to be served, I have kneaded less and more, which does change the texture a bit: less being lighter and more being denser. We also use this recipe to roll out thin and make wraps for hot dogs. Simply roll the dough to 1/4 inch and cut to fit around a hot dog, plus about 1/4 inch (it stretches well if you are a tad short). Overlap the ends, wet the seam, and press to seal well. Place the hot dogs so the seam is at the bottom on top of the cooking sheet. Then finish by following the cooking directions for the biscuits as given in the recipe. There should be plenty to do a package of hot dogs with some left over. We just don't buy hot dog buns anymore!!!

I had never made biscuits from scratch in my life until I made these.  Perfection!!! I put the bowl of dry ingredients into the deep freeze for 30 min before making to ensure it was all cold. Following other suggestions I used 1 teaspoon salt, buttermilk instead of regular milk, and grated frozen butter into the flour instead of shortening. I only kneaded it 4-5 times until I was able to roll it out, then straight into the hot oven. My visiting mother-in-law is a life-long native Texan, and she admitted they were as good as any she has ever had. High praise, from her!

I did something wrong!!!!  My dough was way too wet, maybe my egg was too big?  Not knowing exactly what went wrong, I decided to make the best of the situation and make "drop biscuits" instead.  Turned out fabulous!  They are light as a feather and taste great.  To the bad reviewers that say that they're not wowed by this recipe I say this: this wonderful recipe knows its place and doesn't try to be the star of the show.  It's a great compliment to almost any meal, spread, or topping.  It also services as an alternative to a knife for helping you scoop up food off your plate and it is also good for sopping up gravies and other delectables off your plate.    So again to the people giving this a bad review I think they've got the wrong idea about what a biscuit is suppose to be.  Now that I know what wonderful drop biscuits these make, I plan to make these again and I'll try to reproduce my mistake which was probably putting "too much" milk in it.

I have to admit I was skeptical about these biscuits--especially since there is an egg in them. I must admit I was pleasantly surprised. The egg keeps the biscuits from falling apart as they are very tender. I happened to have butter flavored shortening. It was a good thing because if I had used plain shortening the biscuits would have been tasteless. Another note: at first the dough seemed too sticky and I was tempted to add more flour. The dough ended up sitting for a couple minutes and it set up, it wasn't too sticky to work with anymore. Really great biscuits--I'll probably make them again!

text:
These are really good. I made them as the recipe states, and they turned out really well and are quite tasty, even using the shortening they call for. No, they won't have quite as buttery of a taste if you use shortening instead of butter, but they're still really good. They're also quite easy to make, and you can make a nice biscuit whether you roll and cut them or shape them by hand. (Obviously, the cut ones look a bit tidier and more like "traditional" biscuits.) I'd highly recommend this recipe for a quick, easy, tasty biscuit recipe!

None
text:
Very good. Definitely will make again.  The use of an egg in the biscuit mix was unusual, but a good thing...it helps to give the mix loft and flavor. Some other reviewers have said that the use of shortening in place of butter makes the biscuits lack flavor, but I did not personally think so. I avoided butter due to a dairy insensitivity and felt that the shortening was perfectly fine.  These were easy to make (prep time about 5 mins) and cooking time was as listed. Some hints to consider: use a sharp sided cutter to create loft and make sure your oven is HOT and up to the proper temp. Biscuits like a hot, short cooking time for maximum loft and fluffiness. Also, don't knead the dough much, just enough to bring it together, roll it out (I often just pat it into shape with my hands) and then cut it. More handling makes tougher end results. Use the least amount of flour on your rolling surface that you can get away with using. These things make for the best results.  Enjoy!

Nancy, I would like to thank you so very much for this recipe. I did change 2 small things according to some of the reviews and upped the salt/sugar content and used half shortening and half butter. The reason I want to thank you is because this is EXTREMELY close to the way my mother used to make biscuits for our Saturday morning breakfast or she would make them and put sausage in them and freeze them for quick breakfasts thru the week. I have been trying for a very long time to make biscuits the way she did and just couldn't get it right. My mother passed away due to cancer in 2005 when I was only 24, so I really didn't have an opportunity to get into cooking very much and ask her for the recipes she kept in her mind. This recipe means a lot to me and I appreciate you posting it on this site so that I could find it. I would give it 50 stars for sentimental value if I could...Thank you, again. ~Ambrea

text:
Using half butter flavor shortening and half butter, these are the best and flakiest homemade biscuits we've ever had! My teenage daughter had friends over, and they gobbled them up! I follow the directions as-is, except that I roll them half as thick to begin with, then fold the dough over in half, and roll again lightly to compress. This makes them hold together, but creates a natural split when they're ready to be eaten. They're deluxe topped with butter and honey or with sausage gravy ladled over the top of split biscuits. This recipe works perfectly well with spelt flour as well. This one's a keeper!

These are outstanding biscuits! I've always had problems baking them...they always seem to come out hard and dry. But not these! I made a double batch for my big family, and they were gone that same day! Everyone loved these biscuits, and requested that I make them again! city:
None
region:
None
country:
None
text:
Like the reviewer before me, I have made them several different ways.  I've tried all butter, and half butter half butter flavored shortening.  Just like she stated, the all butter biscuits had a to die for flavor but the consistency was off.  The half half biscuits had the perfect consistency, but the flavor was less desirable. Since I always eat the biscuits with butter and salt or with jam, I prefer having the texture right and supplementing the taste with whatever I put on it. I have tried rolling the dough out and softly patting it out.  I find they rise better when you gently pat the dough to the desired thickness.  Also, I tried kneading 4 times and using a biscuit cutter, kneading 4 times and cutting a strip of dough and tying a knot, kneading 20x and using a biscuit cutter, and kneading 20x and cutting a strip and tying a dough knot.  Contrary to what most people are saying on here, like the reviewer before me, I found the 20x kneaded dough to rise TWICE as high as the 4x kneaded dough, and they were still just as tender and flaky.  With this recipe, I REALLY suggest kneading the full amount - I know that's against your best judgment, but trust me!  Also, the biscuits I tied in a knot shape were much larger and rose better than the disc shaped biscuits. So to sum it all up, for best results, don't skip on the kneading!

This is a great recipe! We have a large family so I always double the recipe. The only critique I have is that it is always a little too sticky/wet. I have to add a lot of flour to the work surface and the rolled dough to get it to be "workable." But they come out very fluffy and flaky. My family loves them! Thanks for the recipe!

Edited to add..... don't overwork these, they will be fluffier and buttery if you only knead a few times, until the dough is together and can be rolled out.  20 times kneading is too much.

Excellent!  I, too, used butter.  I put the dry ingredients into the food processor and pulse a couple of times to "sift" then add cubed cold butter and pulse  a few times again then transfer to a bowl to add the liquid ingredients.  Last time I made these I tried the folding technique explained in the AR article on baking powder biscuits and it worked out really nice. If you're pressed for time, you can make these ahead, shape and place on baking pan and put in fridge until ready to bake, however when I do this I usually have to double the baking time.

Absolutely gorgeous biscuits. I have only ever used [a popular baking mix] to make biscuits but I live in Scotland now and it's very hard to find it in the shops. In desperation, I thought I'd try to find a recipe that would allow me to bake reasonable biscuits, never expecting that they would be BETTER than the ones from the mix. 

To quote the family, these are: "Brilliant!" (the 8-year-old) "Delicious!" (the 11-year-old) "magnificent" (the 42-year-old). lol 

I did have a moment's pause when I got the dough mixed up, as it was very sticky and I couldn't imagine how I would manage to roll it out (I'm not much of a cook). However, I followed the instructions, applied a lot of flour to the outside and it turned into the loveliest dough. A bit of kneading, rolling and cutting out and we had perfect biscuits that baked up flaky and soft on the inside and buttery-crispy on the outside. Delicious. Sorry, I know I'm raving but...seriously. Great recipe.  I don't think we'll be going back to the mix.

text:
I forgot  the salt and didn't knead them long enough, but these were great!  The best biscuit recipe I've found yet!  

I know people say not to over work biscuit dough or else it will become too dense, which is true (I make biscuits at work every morning) you do need to work the dough *some* so that they'll rise.  My first few wound up being two inch biscuits when they came out of the oven.  But after re-working the dough once more, they were perfect and tall!  

On a side note:  in my opinion, you don't need to knead the dough-- pressing it out and folding the edges in to make a loaf shape a few times is all it needs. All-out kneading (in my experience) can ruin the texture and the volume, depending on how it's done.

text:
I believe this is the first time I ever made biscuits!  A warning to anyone else with limited biscuit experience - the "dough" is very sticky prior to the kneeding step.  So use a lot of flour on your hands and the surface you plop your dough onto.  I am assuming the sticky-dough-aspect is normal for biscuits because they turned out great.  I used half white flour and half wheat flour.  Half butter flavored shortening and half real butter.  Substituted garlic salt for the salt.  Used my heart-shaped cookie cutter for an extra "cute".  Baked in 400 degrees on my airbake cookie sheet for 20 minutes.   

Next time I am going to add a little cheddar cheese to the mix!  Overall great recipe to get me started!

city:
None
region:
None
country:
None
text:
I did modify this recipe.  My family doesn't eat anything with hydrogenated oils, so I replaced the shortening with butter.  I also replaced the milk with buttermilk.    There is a trick to using butter with biscuits that doesn't just apply to this recipe....  If you switch to butter, you must soft freeze the butter by tossing it in the freezer for 20 mins or so.  If it melts while you are kneading it, the biscuits will just be greasy and not flaky at all.  I threw all of the ingredients into the food processor with the cutting blade, and pulsed it until it formed a rough ball, about 45 seconds to one minute.  Then rolled out out *quickly* folding it over about 4 times, and then cut with minimal handling.  The more you handle it, the more the butter will melt.  If you don't have a food processor, you can grate the frozen butter and then knead it in by hand.  If you do this method, you have to make sure your milk and egg are COLD and you must work quickly.  Brushing the tops with melted butter before baking will give a really nice golden top also.  Best biscuit recipe I've ever had.  And I think I have tried almost every one out there.

This is one I have on my fridge and use all the time.  However, I've tweaked it a little over the years.  I only use 3tsp baking powder so the biscuits aren't so dry.  I always use butter instead of shortening though so that's probably why I had to tweak.  I also do a full TBSP of sugar.  These are great and easy, perfect for sausage gravy or as their own side with roast beef or chicken noodle soup... thank you!

text:
These are the BEST biscuits I've ever made!  They melt in your mouth!  Instead of all shortening, I used 1/4 cup shortening and 1/4 cup cold butter.  Then, as suggested by another user, I kneaded about 5 times, lightly patted out flat, and folded over 4 times to make layers. I really think this made all the difference in producing very light and fluffy biscuits.  My husband raved about them, too, and told me to use this recipe for our biscuits in the future!  THANKS SO MUCH FOR POSTING THIS ONE!!!

text:
YUM. Love these biscuits. I used all butter, no shortening. I thought the flavor from using all butter was Fantastic. (who keeps shortening on hand these days?) I enjoyed the texture of these biscuits, I thought they came out great. I did knead the second batch I made, and they rose VERY high. When using all butter, I found the dough to be very sticky, so I just added a little extra flour and it came out perfect. Alternatively you could just use a little less milk. This is the best biscuit recipe I have found yet!

**edit to add: I have been trying to count my calories to help lose weight. FYI, these have 161 calories per biscuit when using butter, more when using shortening. I used the caloriecount recipe analysis.

text:
These were good!  I used 1 t. salt, 1/4 c. shortening, 1/4 c. COLD butter diced in small cubes.  The dough is sticky - resist the urge to handle it roughly or too much.  (Flour your board and have some extra flour on hand.)  Lightly kneaded about 20 times, rolled to 3/4" thick and then cut with a floured water glass into 4 rounds, gathered the remaining dough together and shaped into a rounds.  (I didn't re-roll.)  The last two didn't look the same, but they tasted the same!  They rose to about 2 inches after baking 8 minutes - golden on top and bottom.  I posted a pic.

Hmm.. These were just okay. I guess I fall into the group of people who thought that these were a bit bland. They were very beautiful, but just didn't taste like much. I only kneaded these about 5-6 times, not 20, that would have been way too many. That is why some peoples have come out so dense. I also used 1/4 butter 1/4 shortening. It's too bad, because I made these to show an English friend what "real American biscuits" are, and I sort of feel like I should have just bought some Grands.

text:
Just what I have been looking for - these were much better than another baking soda recipe I tried. Based on a reviewer's suggestion, I used one 1/4 cup shortening and one 1/4 cup butter. And to make it easier, I just kneaded the dough in the bowl and then used a 1/4 cup measuring cup to scoop it out and place on the cookie sheet. This made less 'perfectly-formed' biscuits, but if you don't care about perfect uniformity, then this is an easier (and cleaner!) way than rolling them out. Lastly, I used buttermilk instead of milk, and brushed buttermilk on the tops before putting them in the oven. I served them with chili con carne, and they were perfect!

I thought these were great, considering how easy they are to whip up.  I used half cold butter and half shortening, like one reviewer suggested and made sure I had plenty of clumps in the dough for flakiness.  I patted my dough out to about one inch in thickness (instead of rolling) and used a 3" diameter glass to cut out six huge biscuit.  I cooked them for two minutes longer because of their size.  I'll definitely make these again whenever I need a biscuit recipe that doesn't require ingredients I don't normally have on hand.

text:
This is almost identical to the flaky biscuit recipe, that I came up with.  Only difference is I use more buttermilk and this one calls for sugar and an egg.  So today I made mine and this 1.  Then had my 4 kids taste test them, they said mine is great for stew toppers, gravy, jelly, plain, or as a cheddar biscuit.  This version  is good for jelly, plain, served as side to fried chicken, as a cheddar biscuit or dessert biscuit.  I did up the buttermilk to equal what my other version uses to have them come out. In doing so I got 12 -1in thick pre-cooked biscuits.  With my adjustments I will be making both types of biscuit (my flaky and this fluffy) in the future.  Thanks for sharing would of never thought to add sugar and an egg to what I already knew was a great recipe. :) Although since I did change it, I can't give this recipe more then 3 stars.

Prepared as written and enjoyed a most excellent biscuit. This is a biscuit that doesn't require drinking a gallon of milk before you can physically resume normal speech. Super fast and easy. Light crispiness on the outside and soft and fluffy on the inside. Dont worry that the dough is so loose before turning out. The flour on the kneading surface will use up the liquid quickly. Awesome with strawberry jam. Family approved.

text:
I just made this for me and my girlfriend, we are big fans of this recipe.  First thing to note, I did alter the recipe as one reviewer suggested by putting 1/4 cup shortening, and 1/4 cup butter.  The biscuits came out very fluffy and taste great with butter and maple syrup!  **Warning** Do not over bake.  These will burn quickly.  Our biscuits did not brown much, so we left it in there for 10 min. and half of them burned on the bottom.  So I would suggest taking them out at the 8 minute mark and making sure they are not burned.

These were amazing!  Helpful hints:  
I did as others suggested and used half butter and half shortening.  The flavor was great.
I put all of the dry ingredients in the food processor and pulsed for a few seconds to blend in the butter and shortening.  I added the milk and egg until just combined.  I rolled between wax paper because the dough was sticky.  It was a little messy, but easy to remove from the wax paper.  Adding too much flour will make biscuits come out too dry.... great, simple recipe!

text:
I made a double batch and substituted the crisco for all butter, it barely had flavor. And the dough was so sticky that no matter how much flour I put down it kept sticking to the counter. That's another thing- the flour taste is overpowering and the biscuits came out quite dry. I tried to stack 2 circles of dough and pinch the sides together in hope that they'd bake together and be much more fluffy. No luck- instead they baked as 2 complete biscuits with 1 side of each not being done at all. Many of them came out like small, hard hockey pucks. With the last remaining circles I had completely redone and squished into large balls of dough. They did come out higher and fluffier but still a strong flour taste. USE HONEY AND BUTTER OR JELLY/JAM to top them. Then atleast you get some flavor. I had to cook each tray full for 12mins and I give this recipe 2 stars for lack of expectations.

text:
Best biscuit recipe I've used and will continue to use. Took other people's comments and modified the original recipe slightly by doing 1/4 c. shortening and 1/4 c. butter and upped the salt to 3/4 tsp. Also didn't knead the dough too much - maybe 10 times vs. the 20 that was called for - and I didn't roll out the dough just patted it out on my floured board to about 1" thick and cut with a drinking glass then brushed the tops with a little melted butter. Came out very flaky, nice flavor, and rose very nicely! Tasted great with the beef stew I made! Thanks!!

text:
I made these biscuits today for breakfast and had a couple of problems.  I had no shortening so, after reading other reviews, I used cold butter.  The dough was very sticky and I found I had to keep adding flour so I could work with it.  The biscuits did not rise very much at all, but, the end result was still a light, tasty biscuit.  I then took the leftover dough, patted it into a 1/4 inch high rectangle and spread it with margarine.  I then sprinkled sugar and cinnamon on top, rolled it into a tube, cut it into inch and a half slices, and baked them in a 450 degree oven for about 10-12 minutes. We drizzled them with a confectioner sugar glaze, and they were fantastic!  I don't think this will be my go to recipe for biscuits, but I will definitely use it for making cinnamon swirls!!  Thanks for a great recipe!

I made these today for my boyfriend when he came over for lunch with some fried chicken. The biscuits turned out amazingly! I doubled the recipe and rolled the dough out 1" thick. text:
First time ever making biscuits, here is what I learned:  *Use 1/2 butter & 1/2 shortening I'm sure it tastes a lot better this way. *If your butter has salt cut back on the recipe's.  My butter had salt... so I learned. *Don't knead 20 times.  I did and they weren't so fluffy. *Don't wait for them to be golden once they are in the oven unless you've spread something on them. *Add the liquid very slowly or it will go terribly wrong. Will make again I loved them very much.

Absolutely the best biscuits I've ever made or tasted.  These came together so easily and tasted so soft and mild.  I had them for breakfast with the pumpkin butter (from this site) and they were FANTASTIC.  Note, I didn't roll these out and cut them. I cannot make a biscuit..but I thought I'd give it one more try. First time they were good, I substituted butter for the shortning, and I was fairly pleased with the results. Second time, I used whole wheat flour and the shortening and I was again reminded I have no business making biscuits.lol I thought the dough was on the dry side so the third time I used margarine instead of shortening, added about a 1/3 c extra milk, used regular flour and these were biscuits to die for. Didn't rise as high as I would like, but I rolled it out on the thinner side, so that was my fault.  So tender and such a good flavor.  Now, if only I could get homemade bread to not turn out like something you would use for a doorstop ;-}

I LOVED these!  Hubby thought they were "okay."  Biscuit-loving 10-yr-old ate only one, but he strongly prefers canned biscuits.  I love these because they came out flakey, tender and were somewhat bland but didn't taste like flour.  The benefit of a bland biscuit is being able to use it for whatever purpose you want without a baked-in flavor interfering with the end result.  IE: I don't put butter on the biscuit to make a breakfast sandwhich, nor to use with sausage gravy, nor when eating them with certain soups.  This recipe definitely replaces the one I've been using for many years.

text:
Update: I've made these several times and I can tell you that the best way is this: 
1. Use salted butter instead. 
2. Do not cut in the butter til it resembles crumbs. Cut it in til it's about the size of small peas/half a pea. 
3. Do NOT need it what so ever. After cutting the butter in, pour the milk & egg mixture over the dry and stir til it just comes together. 
4. Dump the biscuit mixture onto a floured surface, sprinkle with flour and then pat it flat to about 3/4 of an inch thick. 
5. Cut the biscuits as desired and bake 8 minutes, remove and let rest. 
These are the keys to getting TENDER, FLAKY biscuits that have a good flavor. The original instructions are good, but if you make these changes the biscuits are wonderful. Note: I usually cut my dough into wedges like scones. 

Original Review: As other suggested, I used butter instead of shortening. But I do that with pretty much all recipes. I'm not a fan of shortening at all. The most I go is 50/50 on a recipe. Anyway... I added a bit of pepper to the recipe because I was using the biscuits to top a casserole. Other than the pepper and butter I followed the recipe closely. I used an organic egg and skim milk and kneaded it about 25 times. I oiled the top with some grape seed oil and they turned out delicious. Golden brown. Light. Tender. So tender. They were PERFECT with the casserole filling (ground lean turkey+mixed veggies+can of golden mushroom soup+minced onions+herbs+S&P). Family wolfed it down with pleasure!

city:

region:
None
country:
None
text:
To start, I made a double batch(wanted plenty of tasting). I used half, salted- butter/half margerine, cut the sugar by 1 teaspoon, added 1 1/2 teaspoon lemon juice. Baked at 400/410F/27ft elevation. I am very pleased with the soft mealy-texture(crumbly, not flaky), high-rise(started at 1" raised to nearly 3". The spreading the dough by hand and folding 20 times brings great results. The big plus for me is that these biscuits don't leave a slick/greasy feel in the mouth(ate 5 in a row). The finished biscuit bakes-up squaty(larger at the bottom), but in no way is un-attractive. I tried a few right out of the oven, the texture is dense and over-moist, I prefer them at room temp. the feel in the mouth is so inviting and leads to reaching for many more.

text:
I made almost this recipe, except that I did some research on making biscuits.  The article claimed that using 1 cup of regular flour and 1 cup of cake flour would make a great deal of different.  The fat ratio is 1/2 cup for every two cups of "flour".  I used unsalted butter the first time and it was so bland!  The second time I used salted butter and 1/2 tsp. of salt.  My recipe didn't call for egg, but did call for buttermilk.  I made the "homemade" version of buttermilk (milk and vinegar).  They were the best biscuit I've ever made, but I'm still looking for a biscuit that reminds me of BoB Evans biscuits.  I'd kill for that recipe!
